A future to believe in!

One could forgive practically every voter in the country, yourself included, for being shocked. Two years ago, pollsters hardly included you in the race. When you declared your candidacy, most articles made sure to highlight that you were a long shot. Why wouldn’t they? You were going up against Hillary Clinton. And yet, you said it best in a quote added as an addendum to most of those articles at the bottom of the page:

‘I think people should be a little bit careful underestimating me'

Now, you have managed, despite it all, despite the primaries, despite running as a third party candidate in a country where one hasn’t won a state since the sixties, to outright win more than 270 votes in the electoral college. And not just that: you won comfortably when near-every outlet predicted a contingent election, at best.

No, believe it one cannot. Your opponents hardly offer a concession the day of, likely unable to believe their eyes; they’re joined by your wife, Jane, by your supporters, awestruck to what can only be described as a political revolution.

The Republican Party has already declared its response to your victory: the newly debuted Fox host, Tucker Carlson, declares that an undemocratic communist revolution has taken hold of the United States. ‘The Bolsheviks have just stormed the Winter Palace,’ he declares , ‘and we cannot stand by.’ The Democratic Party, meanwhile, has reacted with pure confusion. Some certainly want to work with you: after all, the most left-wing President of the United States has just won: what else is there to do? Others, chiefly Hillary, have behind the scenes pushed something else (from what you’ve heard,) and she’s joined by other influential voices.

  

If you would like, you certainly have an opening to stage a takeover of the Democratic Party, perhaps starting next year with the DNC chairmanship, but be warned: this is a party that his been incredibly hostile to you, and many of those likely to support you have been pushed out. Several leftists have managed to join Congress, a few even winning outside of the two parties, such as Gayle McLaughlin of the Greens. It is only a handful though: not enough to exert control, although shockingly, Democrats have managed to take both Houses of Congress, likely thanks to Trump backed third parties. It may not be enough to pass Medicare For All, but that's for you to negotiate.

Regardless, you will be America’s first socialist President, come January. You will at least have four years, and re-election might be in the cards, but who knows in what form? There will likely be an attempt to change the electoral system of this country after what happened this year, but you will likely have a role in that as well. The world watches as you start packing for Washington.

If you listen, you can hear a whisper.

You have made the top three, an achievement in and of itself, joining Hillary but, surprisingly, Donald Trump. Republican operators seethe as Donald Trump defiantly declares that he will become the next President of the United States, and that Republican Congressional leaders should be honored to join him. They’re in a tough spot, but McConnell and Ryan may be forced to tilt that way, for lack of an alternative. And who knows if they can get that done, and what it means for you?

On that note, the race for the Presidency has another turn, as Democrats have, despite the odds being stacked against them, taken both the Senate and, shockingly, the House of Representatives (likely thanks to Trump). Odder still, with Hillary in third, the Senate picks between Ben Carson and Marcy Kaptur. While leadership on both sides is essentially trapped into pulling for their respective anti-establishment candidate, a coalition of moderates from both sides threaten to abstain, forcing the next President to pick a moderate. With Democrats in the Senate majority, the favor is with Kaptur, as she is certainly more palatable to most Democrats. A deadlock is certainly possible, though.

Meanwhile, soon-to-be House Speaker Nancy Pelosi is considering her options. Some have voiced before the election that she could change the rules to only require a plurality of votes to win a state delegation, but that’s only helpful if Trump and Rubio are in the race. There is the chance that moderate Republicans abandon Trump — and if that happens, Hillary has a shot at victory. She might, albeit incredibly reluctantly, need your help, Whether she makes that phone call now, or in January, is up to her, but in the meantime you will certainly be talking to plenty of members of Congress.

  

Regardless, there’s a long time until January. Hillary might attempt to negotiate with you, she might not. It’s not like she has many other options, but she may cite your lack of widespread Congressional support to refuse — in addition to the escalating blame for supposedly spoiling the election against her, sure to pick up if Trump somehow wins. Plenty of things can happen before that, so buckle up: it’s going to be a long few weeks.

The race rolls on.

It was obvious in the month leading up to the election, despite its twists and turns, that the likely outcome was a contingent vote. It’s not surprising that it’s exactly what happened. It’s two months before Congress is scheduled to vote for president and Vice President, and there will certainly be ample politicking in the meantime.

You have made the top three, an achievement in and of itself, alongside Clinton and Rubio. One major candidate has missed it: Donald Trump gave a long speech in the aftermath of election night, declaring the election ‘stolen’ and shouting that yourself, Hillary, and Marco somehow conspired to keep him out of the race. It’s obviously absurd, but there are more important things to be worried about, and your team is already calling any potentially friendly members of Congress ahead of January.

On that note, the race for Congress has gone strangely, as Democrats have taken back four Senate seats, taking the chamber to a tie. With you in third, the Senate picks between Tim Kaine and John Kasich, which is expected to be a party-line vote. If no Senator votes against their party, then that would be a tie, one likely unbreakable by Vice President Biden, lawsuit pending. If the nation is left without a Vice President, whoever ascends to office next would likely have to select the next one, who may have to be a moderate given the state of the chamber.

Meanwhile, the House of Representatives is, as expected, in Republican hands. With no Trump, that probably means that Rubio will be elected, as he only needs 26 State delegations to win. There will be frantic talks around the capital until then, but that is a model outcome: a Republican President.

  

Regardless, there’s a long time until January. Hillary might attempt to negotiate with you, she might not.
